  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_47066027-6f8e-4809-a51f-04037b61a87a'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<div id="review_654318271" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/654318271" />
    <a title="Thomas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2018505-thomas"><img alt="Thomas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567953607p2/2018505.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/654318271?book_show_action=true">Jun 29, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Thomas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Thomas" href="/user/show/2018505-thomas">Thomas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Thomas by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/2864718-roof-beam-reader-adam">Roof Beam Reader (Adam)</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=lgbtq">lgbtq</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer654318271" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer324051205057569123">Some books don't deserve ratings. Not because they're just that bad, but because a number cannot encapsulate everything found within their bindings. <i>Dream Boy</i>, for me, is one of those books - what I liked about it is also what prevented me from loving it fully.<br/><br/>First published over ten years ago at a succinct 195 pages, <i>Dream Boy</i> revolves around Nathan, a sophomore in high school who falls into a complex relationship with Roy, a senior. Nathan comes from a troubled home. His alcoholic father exem</span>
  <span id="freeText324051205057569123" style="display:none">Some books don't deserve ratings. Not because they're just that bad, but because a number cannot encapsulate everything found within their bindings. <i>Dream Boy</i>, for me, is one of those books - what I liked about it is also what prevented me from loving it fully.<br /><br />First published over ten years ago at a succinct 195 pages, <i>Dream Boy</i> revolves around Nathan, a sophomore in high school who falls into a complex relationship with Roy, a senior. Nathan comes from a troubled home. His alcoholic father exemplifies sanctimony while his mother wisps around like a leaf. Roy gives him warmth, but at a cost - he doesn't want Nathan to tell anyone about their relationship.<br /><br /><i>Dream Boy</i> is about young adults, but might not be for young adults. Grimsley's writing is concise and almost clinical, yet strongly sensual and violent. His brevity brings Nathan's insecurities and abuse to life. On the surface this book may appear to be about a relationship between two boys, but it has a dark undercurrent and themes that can capture one's mind long after reading.<br /><br />But the blunt nature of this book left me wanting more. There's a difference between an author deciding to leave aspects of his work ambiguous and failing to explore certain characters, motifs, etc. The motives behind why characters would hurt one another or how some of their emotions escalated so quickly could have been further fleshed out.<br /><br />I would recommend this to readers searching for an unusual gay love story with beautiful yet jagged writing. Save this one for later if you're searching for a happy ending - while it has nothing in common with sunshine or prancing unicorns, I promise that it'll make you think.<br /><br />*review cross-posted on my blog, <a href="http://thequietvoice18.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">the quiet voice</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="324051205057569123" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1124007650" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1124007650" />
    <a title="Sofia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14453898-sofia"><img alt="Sofia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1404331721p2/14453898.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1124007650?book_show_action=true">Dec 05, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sofia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sofia" href="/user/show/14453898-sofia">Sofia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9782864244653" href="/book/show/155789.Dream_Boy">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14453898-sofia?shelf=eagerly-read">eagerly-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14453898-sofia?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14453898-sofia?shelf=library">library</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1124007650" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4663860748375106880"><br/><b>Powerful silent imagery.....</b><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1441280734i/16088490._SX540_.png' width='300' height='100' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</blockquote> <br/>Grimsley uses the third person present to tell us this story. So even though we are getting Nathan's point of view, a distance is still created between us and him and him and his world. This distance mirrors the same distance that Nathan needs to be able to survive what he has been through. So with this writing tool Grimsley puts us in the picture by making us feel the distance, the silence, the invisibility, the loneliness, the wariness. The distrust Nathan feel</span>
  <span id="freeText4663860748375106880" style="display:none"><br><b>Powerful silent imagery.....</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1441280734i/16088490._SX540_.png" width="300" height="100" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote> <br>Grimsley uses the third person present to tell us this story. So even though we are getting Nathan's point of view, a distance is still created between us and him and him and his world. This distance mirrors the same distance that Nathan needs to be able to survive what he has been through. So with this writing tool Grimsley puts us in the picture by making us feel the distance, the silence, the invisibility, the loneliness, the wariness. The distrust Nathan feels is even transmitted in our view of Roy. We know Roy through Nathan, and like Nathan I wanted the relationship, Roy, to be something good but like Nathan I could not fully trust that he would not hurt him either.<br><br>Again Grimsley uses his words to create the surreal feel of the last third of the book. This surreal feeling left me unsure what to think, what to believe. He leaves the ending open to different interpretations. My preferred take is the one I'm going to try and take with me. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ what if what happened after Burke found them was a <b>dream</b>. Maybe losing Roy at that moment brought back the memories Nathan strove so hard to supress and his Dad and Burke got all mixed up in a kind of nightmare. After all he always saw Burke as a violent antagonist. So his going back would be a kind of a win as he could have decide to end it there. Roy making a choice at the end between church-girl and Nathan also opens up possibilities. I don't know where they go from here everything is possible. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br><br>It's not the kind of story which makes you happy, because it touches ugly things, this notwithstanding I found it excellently crafted. I admire how Grimsley gave a silent voice to Nathan which I heard loud and clear. All in such a short amount of pages.<br><br><br>BR with Ije <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user_status/show/74913705" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1378812972?comment=139613069#comment_139613069" rel="nofollow noopener">&amp; here</a> and Ira offline </["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="4663860748375106880" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Cristina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10105913-cristina"><img alt="Cristina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1545001055p2/10105913.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2065276703?book_show_action=true">Sep 12, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina" href="/user/show/10105913-cristina">Cristina</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/19164981-dream-boy">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10105913-cristina?shelf=lgbtq">lgbtq</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10105913-cristina?shelf=queer">queer</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10105913-cristina?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2065276703" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer386941413694716999"><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/90090.Jim_Grimsley' title='Jim Grimsley' rel='nofollow noopener'> Jim Grimsley</a>'s wonderful book is conceived of facts and dreams.<br/><br/>Its facts are disturbing and painful - Nathan's abusive father, Burke's violent acts, the brutality of the very environment surrounding Nathan and Roy - conjure up a setting where even the cracking of a floorboard or a light under a door could indicate the onset of violence and abuse. <br/><br/>But there are also dreams in Nathan's small world: his encounters with Roy (despite Roy's demand that they remain a secret) are infused with tendernes</span>
  <span id="freeText386941413694716999" style="display:none"><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/90090.Jim_Grimsley" title="Jim Grimsley" rel="nofollow noopener"> Jim Grimsley</a>'s wonderful book is conceived of facts and dreams.<br /><br />Its facts are disturbing and painful - Nathan's abusive father, Burke's violent acts, the brutality of the very environment surrounding Nathan and Roy - conjure up a setting where even the cracking of a floorboard or a light under a door could indicate the onset of violence and abuse. <br /><br />But there are also dreams in Nathan's small world: his encounters with Roy (despite Roy's demand that they remain a secret) are infused with tenderness and a sense of wonderment and so are the frequent descriptions of the area surrounding their houses where the lake and the cemetery become places lost in time.<br /><br />The way Nathan silently compares the loving gestures shared with Roy with the heinous acts his father forces upon him - and how he desperately tries to hide away his terrifying knowledge - is simply heartbreaking.<br /><br />The novel focuses on small events: a shared drive, a lunch at school, a walk in the woods, but all these occurrences take on the quality of a Southern Gothic fairytale. The atmosphere is suspended, the prose sparse and soft like the carpet of leaves stepped on by Nathan and Roy in their nocturnal wanderings.<br /><br />I've read the whole novel almost holding my breath as if a sudden noise or a crack in my focus could break the fragile spell cast upon the main two characters. The ending, ambiguous but also full of hope, left me speechless.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/220754.Dream_Boy" title="Dream Boy by Jim Grimsley" rel="nofollow noopener"> Dream Boy</a> is a powerful and amazing novel.</span>
  <a data-text-id="386941413694716999" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer89903225" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2464372663722497814"> Dream Boy is a good beginnng for a novel. It's a decent outline. But aside from an intriguing writing style, this book fails if only because there is no ending. <br/><br/>Actually, I felt extremely cheated and angry that the author would do such a thing. First he manipulates us ruthlessly and plays on our emotions and for what? To give us a book with no ending? Either suggested ending is an unbelieveably trite. <br/><br/>The author should be ashamed of himself. Worn out plot, brutal enough to make reading difficul</span>
  <span id="freeText2464372663722497814" style="display:none"> Dream Boy is a good beginnng for a novel. It's a decent outline. But aside from an intriguing writing style, this book fails if only because there is no ending. <br /><br />Actually, I felt extremely cheated and angry that the author would do such a thing. First he manipulates us ruthlessly and plays on our emotions and for what? To give us a book with no ending? Either suggested ending is an unbelieveably trite. <br /><br />The author should be ashamed of himself. Worn out plot, brutal enough to make reading difficult and then absolutely no pay off. <br /><br />And what about all of the missing material and answers to questions raised by the book? What was Burke all about? Why did the father turn from normal to brutal at some point in the boy's life? What drove Roy? Was Nathan gay because his father abused him? And who is this this narrator? <br /><br />An utter waste of time. Much more accomplished gay fiction out there whether you are looking for a coming out story or a story full of brutal challenges for young people. <br /><br />Don't reward this author's barbarism at putting his readers through such trauma for nothing. <br /><br /><br /><br /></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer352801462" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16263920469355427213"><b> Such a brilliant gay fiction book. </b><br/><br/><br/>This was my first gay romance book or gay fiction book, whichever you prefer to call it. I fell in love with it the second I started reading it. It didn't take me very long to read it, because I couldn't put it down, but partly because it was very short, too. It was a very quick read. And I also read it on my 15th birthday, which isn't really relevant... but anyway.<br/><br/>Jim Grimsley did an amazing job with Nathan. He was a shy boy, but he had something inside. It w</span>
  <span id="freeText16263920469355427213" style="display:none"><b> Such a brilliant gay fiction book. </b><br /><br /><br />This was my first gay romance book or gay fiction book, whichever you prefer to call it. I fell in love with it the second I started reading it. It didn't take me very long to read it, because I couldn't put it down, but partly because it was very short, too. It was a very quick read. And I also read it on my 15th birthday, which isn't really relevant... but anyway.<br /><br />Jim Grimsley did an amazing job with Nathan. He was a shy boy, but he had something inside. It was broken but it had the innocence of childhood. Even when he took the lead I could see the childishness in him. It was raw and beautiful to me and the detail in the book was exquisite. We don't get a lot of gory details, but we can see everything and we know what's going on.<br /><br />My main issue with this book was how Roy treated Nathan. It's not exactly a romance, so I guess it's why I was able to enjoy it as much as I did. There was a romance of sorts in the book, but it's more of a gay fiction book or a YA gay fiction book than an m/m romance, which is what I usually read. Still, I did think it was amazing and the writing really brought me in.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16263920469355427213" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_203545100" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Mel Bossa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6164432-mel-bossa"><img alt="Mel Bossa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594654702p2/6164432.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/203545100?book_show_action=true">Aug 30, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mel Bossa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mel Bossa" href="/user/show/6164432-mel-bossa">Mel Bossa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6164432-mel-bossa?shelf=0006-lgbtq">0006-lgbtq</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6164432-mel-bossa?shelf=0008-fiction">0008-fiction</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer203545100" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12985948470897683952">This was my third or fourth read of this magnificent book by Jim Grimsley. This is the book I return to when I want to be inspired to write better. <br/><br/>This was my first reaction to Dream boy, in 2010, when I first read it:<br/><br/>Dream Boy by Jim Grimsley. I read it in an hour and a half. The apartment could have been engulfed in fire. I couldn't care less. I only wanted his words. Only needed to turn the pages.<br/><br/>It has been a very very long and lonely time since I've come across such a kindred soul. His wri</span>
  <span id="freeText12985948470897683952" style="display:none">This was my third or fourth read of this magnificent book by Jim Grimsley. This is the book I return to when I want to be inspired to write better. <br /><br />This was my first reaction to Dream boy, in 2010, when I first read it:<br /><br />Dream Boy by Jim Grimsley. I read it in an hour and a half. The apartment could have been engulfed in fire. I couldn't care less. I only wanted his words. Only needed to turn the pages.<br /><br />It has been a very very long and lonely time since I've come across such a kindred soul. His writing is in tune with a song I've been humming secretly all my life. If I could write a novel like that, I would die at peace with myself.<br /><br />I finished the book.<br /><br />Shut it close.<br /><br />Wept into my hands for five minutes.<br /><br />_______________<br /><br /><br />last night, I couldn't sleep and read Nathan and Roy's story again. I savored every word. It always leaves me aching. This is a Southern voice at its best. This is as powerful as Faulkner, and I won't take that statement back. <br /><br />Nathan is a character I can't and will never forget. The kind of character you think of in the last years of your life, and miss, and wish you'd known in real life.<br /><br />READ THIS BOOK.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12985948470897683952" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1378812972" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1378812972" />
    <a title="Ije the Devourer of Books" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5490353-ije-the-devourer-of-books"><img alt="Ije the Devourer of Books" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1385814164p2/5490353.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1378812972?book_show_action=true">Aug 31, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ije the Devourer of Books" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ije the Devourer of Books" href="/user/show/5490353-ije-the-devourer-of-books">Ije the Devourer of Books</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1378812972" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10938145971227649545">Many thanks to Sofia for buddy reading this with me. I certainly wouldn't have wanted to read it on my own.<br/><br/>This is a melancholy story, poignant, beautifully written but very disturbing. Even the teen gay romance within its pages could not redeem it from the darkness and the violence within it. Everything shimmered with the fragility of first love but shattered into pieces with the violence.<br/><br/>And then the open endedness of the story did not allow for resolution and peace. Although I suppose we can </span>
  <span id="freeText10938145971227649545" style="display:none">Many thanks to Sofia for buddy reading this with me. I certainly wouldn't have wanted to read it on my own.<br /><br />This is a melancholy story, poignant, beautifully written but very disturbing. Even the teen gay romance within its pages could not redeem it from the darkness and the violence within it. Everything shimmered with the fragility of first love but shattered into pieces with the violence.<br /><br />And then the open endedness of the story did not allow for resolution and peace. Although I suppose we can read into the ending what we will.<br /><br />I did look at some of the reviews about this book and I had to wonder.<br /><br />Am I the only person to acknowledge that this is a story about an abused child? I was outraged by the adults in this book - the abuser father, the mother who by her silence collaborated in this abuse and all those people who didn't see or perhaps couldn't have seen the abused teenager in their midst.<br /><br />I just couldn't get over the abuse. It isn't portrayed in any detail but it is implied in the actions and words of the characters. It hovers over the story like some malevolent spirit and that is the impression this story left on me.The abuse overshadowed the teen romance for me and it overshadowed it because I was outraged!<br /><br />I didn't like this story even though I gave it three stars. It left me disturbed and with far too many questions.<br /><br />But funnily enough I enjoyed the writing. It was both poignant and beautiful but with the underlying theme of darkness, violence and abuse. Right from the beginning I knew something was going to happen but for me the darkness when it came was not just from one person. It was present in many of the characters.<br /><br />For me Nathan is the hero in this story. The younger boy caught between the grip of his first love for another boy and the oppressive grip of his abuser of a father. On the face of it this seems like a love story between two teenagers but I felt that Roy ,the love interest, was rather controlling and that his first overtures towards Nathan were bordering on 'grooming'. I know that the hiddeness of the relationship was probably about the fact that it was a gay relationship but the power differential and the way in which Roy had control left me feeling uncomfortable.<br /><br />But not as uncomfortable as the abusing dad!<br /><br />There were clear signs of child abuse. The fact that Nathan seemed to be sexually advanced and was sleeping with his clothes on (in case he had to run) indicated to me that he was abused by his father. So Nathan was caught between two men - his father and Roy, although his father was clearly the abuser. <br /><br />His mother seemed to be powerless but still sympathetic towards her son but she did nothing. She turned a blind eye to the abuse of her son. I wanted to shake her! <br /><br />What I want is justice!! <br /><br />And then maybe I would be happy with two teenagers who would be free from abuse and manipulation to explore their love. That's my ending. <br /><br />Rant over.<br /><br />I gave it three stars. The writing is excellent, well worth five stars or more, but I just didn't enjoy the story so I couldn't give it more stars. The story is very atmospheric. The writing takes you to rural America where 'religion and ritual' supposedly hold sway in the open but in reality is superficial because secrets and darkness hold sway behind closed doors. <br /><br />And so for me this is a story with a dream like surface. It is the kind of writing that reminds me of shimmering summer heat but underneath is the stuff of nightmares, utter darkness, desperation and horror. <br /><br />The religion to me was part of the veneer of respectability and everyone knows full well how child abusers can remain hidden in the guise of respectability not just in church but in any responsible or prominent position in society. <br /><br />So for me there were incredibly dark undertones. I am not sure whether this is what the story is trying to convey or whether I am reading this through a 21st century lens of historic child abuse allegations and child protection procedures. For people who work with children these can make us hyper vigilant which isn't a bad thing but can colour how we see things. <br /><br />And so this is how I have seen the story. Through the eyes of a professional who works with children and is trained to be alert to abusers and to the abused whether children or adults. My dream for this story is that the mother would wake up and take steps to protect her son. That the Father would be arrested and thrown in jail or perhaps have a millstone tied around his neck and be thrown into the sea (just as Jesus suggested for those who abuse children Mark 9:42) and that the bullying and violent teenager be apprehended and also dealt with by the law.<br /><br />I didn't like the ending because it left me feeling unsatisfied. What happened? I guess as a reader I am left to draw my own conclusion. I dislike open ended stories. I like at least a hint of the ending otherwise to me it feels a little like a cop out and I didn't get that ending here. We are left to dream the ending for ourselves. <br /><br />For me it seems as if Nathan was very much alive at the end or maybe he wasn't but whatever happened he gave Roy the chance to leave his small town where horror happens behind closed doors. And Nathan whether alive or dead also managed to escape and move to freedom. Whether alive or dead both boys were able to escape to freedom.<br /><br />And for that I am grateful.<br /><br /><br />But I definitely will not be watching the film!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10938145971227649545" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Nancy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/113545-nancy"><img alt="Nancy" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/204221307?book_show_action=true">Sep 01, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nancy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nancy" href="/user/show/113545-nancy">Nancy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer204221307" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer806969323805037184">Wow, I don't know what to make of this. I heard about it on NPR; the commentator, a gay man, said he wished he had had this book when he was a teenager, because it would have told him he was not alone. That seemed a good reason to read it.<br/><br/>Dream Boy follows Nathan, a bright, delicate 15-year-old-boy, as he falls into a dreamlike courtship with Roy, an older, popular boy at Nathan's new school. Though the sex never feels prurient, the novel is unrelentingly sexual. I started to wonder if there was</span>
  <span id="freeText806969323805037184" style="display:none">Wow, I don't know what to make of this. I heard about it on NPR; the commentator, a gay man, said he wished he had had this book when he was a teenager, because it would have told him he was not alone. That seemed a good reason to read it.<br /><br />Dream Boy follows Nathan, a bright, delicate 15-year-old-boy, as he falls into a dreamlike courtship with Roy, an older, popular boy at Nathan's new school. Though the sex never feels prurient, the novel is unrelentingly sexual. I started to wonder if there was a single moment of Nathan's life when he wasn't obsessing about sex - and then I realized that Nathan is a fifteen-year-old boy, so the answer might well be NO.<br /><br />What makes the novel so powerful (and it is powerful) is the haunting sense of doom that hangs over every moment: sex is dangerous to Nathan in ways that I can hardly imagine, and his situation made me want to hurry up and finish the book before everything came crashing down. The relationship between the two boys is poignant, confused, touchingly inarticulate, and haunted by the emotional and physical peril implicit in their bond. The final denouement, which takes place in a haunted house, is both eerie and disturbingly concrete; my conscious mind was going "Wait, what happened there?" while some inner part of me was saying, "I think I get it." But I'm still not sure I do.<br /><br />This is a very short novel, almost a novella; but it's complex, lyrical, disturbing. Worth reading. </span>
  <a data-text-id="806969323805037184" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12836004856100325964">I have mixed feelings on this one, at the start it appealed to me. The story is told from Nathan’s perspective, he just moved to a new town and meets his neighbor Roy. I believe it’s around 1950’s and the story does a nice job of recapturing the time, setting and mindset during that period. Nathan and Roy are a bit different but become good friends instantly, it’s not really explained how but the meet and they become super close. Nathan’s struggles with a difficult family life throughout the sto</span>
  <span id="freeText12836004856100325964" style="display:none">I have mixed feelings on this one, at the start it appealed to me. The story is told from Nathan’s perspective, he just moved to a new town and meets his neighbor Roy. I believe it’s around 1950’s and the story does a nice job of recapturing the time, setting and mindset during that period. Nathan and Roy are a bit different but become good friends instantly, it’s not really explained how but the meet and they become super close. Nathan’s struggles with a difficult family life throughout the story. The book also put en emphasis on the boys religious upbringing and how that influences each of the boys. The writing, in an attempt to create mood was strange and at times confusing. The last 25% of the book IMO just went on a tangent. In an attempt to create an eerie vibe it was long and confusing. The very end of this book left me completely baffled and not in a good way - one that makes you think or question. This one left me thinking that made no sense and WTF?</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_285471321" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/285471321" />
    <a title="Bonnie Brody" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7630898-bonnie-brody"><img alt="Bonnie Brody" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1571268702p2/7630898.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/285471321?book_show_action=true">Feb 28, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bonnie Brody" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bonnie Brody" href="/user/show/7630898-bonnie-brody">Bonnie Brody</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Bonnie by: </span>
      Heard Interview on NPR
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer285471321" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18367567304810566616">Dream Boy is a tender love story that is also sensual and violent. It is the story of two high school boys who fall in love. Roy and Nathan are neighbors and the attraction is immediate and profound. They are secretive and tentative about their relationship but it is intense and astonishing in its power.<br/><br/>Roy and Nathan attend the same high school where Roy is a senior and Nathan is a sophomore. Nathan has just moved to the area. His family moves often because his father can't keep a job and drink</span>
  <span id="freeText18367567304810566616" style="display:none">Dream Boy is a tender love story that is also sensual and violent. It is the story of two high school boys who fall in love. Roy and Nathan are neighbors and the attraction is immediate and profound. They are secretive and tentative about their relationship but it is intense and astonishing in its power.<br /><br />Roy and Nathan attend the same high school where Roy is a senior and Nathan is a sophomore. Nathan has just moved to the area. His family moves often because his father can't keep a job and drinks a lot. Nathan has a horrible home life with secrets and shame that cause him to isolate himself from others. Meeting Roy brings him out of his shell and connects him with others.<br /><br />The writing in this book is beautiful. It sings, massages, touches the heart, and is soulful. The author is not afraid of addressing the boys' relationship in all its aspects and does not focus solely on the sexuality. The boys' friendship, need for each other and Nathan's sense of safety when he is with Roy are important parts of the narrative.<br /><br />I have rarely read a book that touched me so close to my core. The novel addresses the conflicts that both boys feel between their religion and their desires. Both families are regular church attendees in rather fundamentalist congregations.<br /><br />Nathan lives in constant fear of his father. His mother is like an invisible apparition in his life, turning her head the other way as if everything in the house is alright when in actuality it is like a prison camp. Nathan can only feel safe when he is away from the house. Finding Roy is a safe harbor for him and Roy senses that there is some deep and dark secret that Nathan carries but he does not press him for it.<br /><br />I recommend this book to anyone who loves literature. It is a rare find and a deeply full experience. It is one of the best books I have read this year and deserves wide recognition. I wish more authors could write with the poetry and stark awareness of emotions as Jim Grimsley. He has written two other novels and has won awards as both a playwright and novelist. I plan on looking up his other works. I feel privileged to have read this book which I first became aware of during an interview with the author on NPR.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="18367567304810566616" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9651104391060986075">Dream Boy is haunting, in a "I have to re-read it or else it'll drive me crazy" way. But I'm pretty sure that rereading will not give me answers.<br/><br/>It's also haunting because of the subject matter, the constant foreboding feeling and scenes that always stay on this side of gratifying and keep you pushing through the story.<br/><br/><br/>/I'm not even sure if I liked it.   <span id="freeText9651104391060986075" style="display:none">Dream Boy is haunting, in a "I have to re-read it or else it'll drive me crazy" way. But I'm pretty sure that rereading will not give me answers.<br /><br />It's also haunting because of the subject matter, the constant foreboding feeling and scenes that always stay on this side of gratifying and keep you pushing through the story.<br /><br /><br />/I'm not even sure if I liked it. The ending flipped my rating upside down. Because I suck at understanding surrealism and symbolism. I have so many ideas on this ending, but if I tried to articulate them, I would be about as comprehensible and clear as the ending itself. I'm giving this book 4 stars because I <i>assume</i> Jim Grimsley's ideas are smarter than mine. I assume that he actually <i>had</i> an idea for an ending, but obfuscated it really well in symbolism and ambiguity. These are 4 stars worth of benefit of the doubt./<br /><br /><br />I've glimpsed references to interviews with Jim Grimsley where he says the ending of Dream Boy is up for interpretation, but I call bullshit on open ending. I demand answers.<br /><br />This book is prime discussion material. If anyone wants to bounce ideas about it, here's a willing participant!<br /><br />Here's an article that gave me a bit of perspective on Dream Boy: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[It's spoilery though, so might wanna save it for after this book leaves you dazed and questioning what you just read: <br /><a href="http://www.teenlibrariantoolbox.com/2014/06/sexual-violence-inside-and-because-of-the-closet-by-anthony-isom-svyalit-project/" rel="nofollow noopener">by Anthony Isom</a> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bárbara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bárbara" href="/user/show/17896682-b-rbara">Bárbara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1751464609" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13306664703310254279">There is something that renders me in awe, sometimes: there will be, occasionally, a book I will stumble upon, that will hit me with such strength that will threaten to shake everything that makes me. <br/><br/>This book is one of those cases. <br/><br/> I didn't really expect it to affect me so much; I guess I never imagined it would matter that much, it was supposed to be just another book I had been meaning to read for some time and only now I was getting myself to do it. <br/><br/><br/>I wish I had the words to explain in ful</span>
  <span id="freeText13306664703310254279" style="display:none">There is something that renders me in awe, sometimes: there will be, occasionally, a book I will stumble upon, that will hit me with such strength that will threaten to shake everything that makes me. <br /><br />This book is one of those cases. <br /><br /> I didn't really expect it to affect me so much; I guess I never imagined it would matter that much, it was supposed to be just another book I had been meaning to read for some time and only now I was getting myself to do it. <br /><br /><br />I wish I had the words to explain in full detail every shade of emotion that I got to experience with this book. It's not the first I read of its kind, but it was definitely unique. I can confidently say I'll be adding this to my mental list of favorites. <br /><br />It was a very heavy read, there was so much tension everywhere, at all times... It was definitely something special. It was brilliant. It was beautiful even in its harshness; and what made it even harder for me to stomach, so to speak, was that- even though it takes place during the 70's-, some of the themes are horribly relevant even today. <br /><br />I- I don't know how to explain properly what this book really means. I guess you will have to read it to make sense of its greatness. Please, do. <br /><br />EDIT: I read some comments complaining about the ending being confusing. I'm not going to spoil it for anyone, but for me it was pretty clear. After all, what the author did with the narrative voice there isn't unheard of. I can think about at least ONE other book that uses the same narrative technique, with a similar (or is it the same?) outcome. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Think about what happens at the end of Song Of Achilles by Madeline Miller. Patroclus remains the narrator even after he dies.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>
  <a data-text-id="13306664703310254279" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_103569313" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/103569313" />
    <a title="Nadine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1584031-nadine"><img alt="Nadine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546439310p2/1584031.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/103569313?book_show_action=true">May 20, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nadine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nadine" href="/user/show/1584031-nadine">Nadine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer103569313" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15465183399443717333">Just finished it and am trying to determine what I think. As an atheist bordering the agnostic I am not one for Bible-reading and hymn-singing and so forth. So I cannot read the ending in a religious context. But what remains then? If I say it is about love between Nathan and Roy, then I get the ending (even though it can be seen as over the top, too faitytale-ish or whatever). I get it nonetheless. <br/><br/>I am highly disturbed by the whole plot because the writing gets to you. It seems to be clinical,</span>
  <span id="freeText15465183399443717333" style="display:none">Just finished it and am trying to determine what I think. As an atheist bordering the agnostic I am not one for Bible-reading and hymn-singing and so forth. So I cannot read the ending in a religious context. But what remains then? If I say it is about love between Nathan and Roy, then I get the ending (even though it can be seen as over the top, too faitytale-ish or whatever). I get it nonetheless. <br /><br />I am highly disturbed by the whole plot because the writing gets to you. It seems to be clinical, curt, does not let you out of its grip and does not use overtly poetic images. It hammers the plot into you. With. Precise. Sentences. That's why I couldn't stop reading.<br /><br />I also 'loved' that Nathan's parents were just Mom and Dad. That made them distant, cold. I don't now why but if they had been Mr. and Mrs as the narrator talked about them, they would have had more substance. As it was they had not. They were symbols of failure and abuse. <br /><br />See how I'm struggling to phrase what I want to say while all the while feeling the need to say something? <br /><br />Maybe this is one of those 'controversial' books one has to read for oneself. Because maybe each picks out something personal which won't let them go. For me it is Nathan's desperation and tenderness. And Roy's fear and how they struggle to find themselves in each other. But still I am not sure that the ending is a happy one. <br /><br />I have to think about it some more and leave thus vague.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15465183399443717333" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15405687926232172723">***WARNING FOR SPOILERS***<br/><br/>Ugh, this book kills. It's so beautiful, every single word is perfectly chosen, this isn't a novel it is a work of art!<br/><br/>It starts out as more of a romance - and you do have to dig a little for stuff to like about Roy. The film comes into its own here, as Max Roeg does a great job of showing his vulnerability: the difficulty he has with his peers and trying to maintain his macho image.   <span id="freeText15405687926232172723" style="display:none">***WARNING FOR SPOILERS***<br /><br />Ugh, this book kills. It's so beautiful, every single word is perfectly chosen, this isn't a novel it is a work of art!<br /><br />It starts out as more of a romance - and you do have to dig a little for stuff to like about Roy. The film comes into its own here, as Max Roeg does a great job of showing his vulnerability: the difficulty he has with his peers and trying to maintain his macho image. Also, Roy's love of ghost stories is total love ('this one's true, I swear it').<br /><br />The transition, about halfway through, brings more of a spiritual feel to it and really ramps up the tragedy and the tension. Nathan's abuse at the hands of his father, his mother's inability to protect him, the difficulties of his continuing relationship with Roy and the homophobia and abuse from his and Roy's peers.<br /><br />I think it depends on your beliefs as to how you view the ending. I much prefer the book ending to the film ending. I know not everyone agrees with my thoughts on it, and it is meant to be ambiguous so there is no real right and wrong on what your personal take is.</span>

This is the kind of book I hope to write someday. Told with such brevity but maintaining a thematic power that really hits home with the final sentences of the novel. Incredibly well done. <br/><br/>"By now the pond and cemetery are familiar landmarks, and Nathan knows by certain signs--the particular twist of a </span>
  <span id="freeText16657186506230580341" style="display:none">There's so much tenderness to this story, but also violence, and the third person present tense really made sense to me by the end, as perhaps it was the only logical choice for Grimsley to make. This is the kind of book I hope to write someday. Told with such brevity but maintaining a thematic power that really hits home with the final sentences of the novel. Incredibly well done. <br /><br />"By now the pond and cemetery are familiar landmarks, and Nathan knows by certain signs--the particular twist of a branch, the bend of the creek that runs through the woods here--that they are following the path to the Indian mound. Roy's long strides set an easy pace and his silence engulfs Nathan so that both move with attention to quiet. The country thereabouts is haunted with memories of the courtship between the boys, and near the creekbed they look at each other. 'Don't say anything about that,' Roy warns, but he is laughing when he says it" (110). </span>

<div id="review_346847760" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/346847760" />
    <a title="Andrew" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9726637-andrew"><img alt="Andrew" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1490774908p2/9726637.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/346847760?book_show_action=true">Jun 12, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andrew" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andrew" href="/user/show/9726637-andrew">Andrew</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9726637-andrew?shelf=never-finished">never-finished</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer346847760" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13665825750230439489"><p>This is the first time in a long time that I've had to actually stop a book before I've finished, so I'm not even sure why I'm putting this review up here, but mostly to clear up some things that I feel are important. I tried very hard to just keep charging through the book until it was done, but this book was just that bad. I don't understand how this won an award at all. </p><br/><p>First of all, everything about this novel is repetitive and boring. After the first time they meet, Nathan and Roy basically</p></span>
  <span id="freeText13665825750230439489" style="display:none"><p>This is the first time in a long time that I've had to actually stop a book before I've finished, so I'm not even sure why I'm putting this review up here, but mostly to clear up some things that I feel are important. I tried very hard to just keep charging through the book until it was done, but this book was just that bad. I don't understand how this won an award at all. </p><br /><p>First of all, everything about this novel is repetitive and boring. After the first time they meet, Nathan and Roy basically become "buddies" and every time Roy wants an easy lay he goes to Nathan and they get it on. If I missed any other part of the relationship, forgive me, but literally all I could get out of this couple is that they were fuck buddies and I hadn't read a single thing that wasn't about either of them getting turned on.</p><br /><p>Secondly, what really bothered me was not even the fact that this content was in the book, but the fact it was never mentioned in top reviews or the summary of this book when I was looking into reading it. A huge part of this book revolves around rape and sexual abuse. The book is hinting at Nathan's father's sexual abuse towards him all throughout the book, and when Burke is about to force Nathan to perform sexually with him is when I finally closed this book and said "NOPE. This is ridiculous". Perhaps this book is for you if rape stories are something that you are interested in reading about, and I don't mind seeing small mentions of rape in books since sadly it's something that occurs daily, but the way it was used in this book so often was starting to make me uncomfortable, the biggest problem being the detail. </p><br /><p>Lastly, what bugged me about this book, is that whenever Nathan wasn't performing or thinking about some sort of sexual experience, there was an endless, boring description of things around him like trees, the pond, the barn, his room, the graveyard, ect. That's what was also turning me away from this book was the fact that aside from sexual experience there was literally nothing else going on at all.</p><br /><p>Basically, I don't think this book was much of anything at all, and it's kind of a shame that I'd been interested in this book expecting something different. I guess I'll have to pay more attention into reviews next time. Perhaps if I ever do feel the need to know what else happens, I can look into the movie, but that's most definitely not happening anytime soon.</p></span>
  <a data-text-id="13665825750230439489" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alex" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alex" href="/user/show/888773-alex">Alex</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781565121065" href="/book/show/381293.Dream_Boy">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/888773-alex?shelf=queer">queer</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/888773-alex?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer119055287" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1942811068057226583">Stars: 2.5/5<br/><br/><b>Overall:</b><br/>While this is a beautifully written story with several positive points, the ending really sours the entire story for me.<br/><br/><b>What I liked</b><br/>Writing. The style is unique and moving, feeling abstract and distant in many cases, which works to illustrate how the main character has become closed off (although the writing style doesn't change as he opens up.<br/><br/>Abuse. The main character's relationship with his father is handled well. The fear is palpable without showing any actual abuse being </span>
  <span id="freeText1942811068057226583" style="display:none">Stars: 2.5/5<br /><br /><b>Overall:</b><br />While this is a beautifully written story with several positive points, the ending really sours the entire story for me.<br /><br /><b>What I liked</b><br />Writing. The style is unique and moving, feeling abstract and distant in many cases, which works to illustrate how the main character has become closed off (although the writing style doesn't change as he opens up.<br /><br />Abuse. The main character's relationship with his father is handled well. The fear is palpable without showing any actual abuse being committed, just threats (which is enough). <br /><br /><b>What didn't work</b><br />The ending. I'm not sure if I'm missing something, I didn't read carefully enough, or it's just the style of the book, but the ending was extremely confusing. I'm not exactly sure what happened, and I'm not certain if I'm supposed to know if certain things happened. I found it frustrating to feel uncertain and confused about the ending.<br /><br />Boyfriend. We have an obviously limited view of what other people think and feel, but the main characters "boyfriend" had several moments where I really disliked him. He had a girlfriend, he's hot and cold, he's almost cruel in some instances. While I can understand this logically, I never felt his behaviors were satisfactorily explained or defended. It wasn't until the end that he both ruined and redeemed himself.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1942811068057226583" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('gAd+TeIrFDwTkkMdwgZssxHepvHk4+irfOBXT+ObRKEKfruM/e0xNtjsHFsy9cftcFNAq5qnCJVkoQ+74RG0BA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('QpMwp9CeCo/eR3VPh2rlEnG8AKtf+GF1W4jabsbaaErI6vVmz1gvhRU5Kgl3mU5MEDHm8SG8gUtDyYKaxFCY7w==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

A tough, lonely ex-Marine of 39, Harlan has never allowed himself to love another man. \n\nThen Billy Sive, a brilliant young runner, shows up on his doorstep. He and his two comrades, Vince Matti and Jacques LaFont, were just thrown off a major team for admitting they are gay. Harlan knows that, with proper training, Billy could go to the \'76 Olympics in Montreal.       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/90090.Jim_Grimsley">About Jim Grimsley</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/90090.Jim_Grimsley"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1235984385p3/90090.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/90090.Jim_Grimsley">Jim Grimsley

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer12082696271541389518">Jim Grimsley was born in rural eastern North Carolina and was educated at the University of North Carolina at Chapel Hill, studying writing with Doris Betts and Max Steele. He has published short stories and essays in various quarterlies, including <i>DoubleTake</i>, <i>New Orleans Review</i>, <i>Carolina Quarterly</i>, <i>New Virginia Review</i>, the <i>LA Times</i>, and the <i>New York Times Book Review</i>. Jim’s first novel <i>Winter Bir</i></span>
  <span id="freeText12082696271541389518" style="display:none">Jim Grimsley was born in rural eastern North Carolina and was educated at the University of North Carolina at Chapel Hill, studying writing with Doris Betts and Max Steele. He has published short stories and essays in various quarterlies, including <i>DoubleTake</i>, <i>New Orleans Review</i>, <i>Carolina Quarterly</i>, <i>New Virginia Review</i>, the <i>LA Times</i>, and the <i>New York Times Book Review</i>. Jim’s first novel <i>Winter Birds</i>, was published in the United States by Algonquin Books in the fall of 1994. <i>Winter Birds</i> won the Sue Kaufman Prize for best first novel from the American Academy of Arts and Letters and was a finalist for the PEN/Hemingway Award. He has published other novels, including <i>Dream Boy</i>, <i>Kirith Kirin</i>, and <i>My Drowning</i>. His books are available in Hebrew, German, French, Spanish, Dutch, Italian, Japanese, and Portuguese. He has also published a collection of plays and most recently a memoir, <i>How I Shed My Skin</i>. His body of work as a prose writer and playwright was awarded the Academy Award in Literature from the American Academy of Arts and Letters in 2005. For twenty years he taught writing at Emory University in Atlanta.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12082696271541389518" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
